## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force is a nonlinear function of position x and may include explicit time-dependent driving forces. The acceleration dv_dt typically combines nonlinear restoring terms in x with possible periodic forcing in t.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinearity in restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (forced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (cubic nonlinearity with periodic driving)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Forced pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (sinusoidal restoring + periodic drive)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order Duffing)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Driven nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Duffing with sinusoidal drive)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Damped driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (full Duffing with phase)
- Rational restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) (saturating nonlinear spring)
- Combined forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (multi-frequency driving)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power polynomial restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) indicate symmetric potential wells typical of Duffing-type oscillators
- Even-power terms in position (x²) indicate asymmetric potential wells or broken symmetry in the oscillator
- Periodic functions of time (sin/cos of t) indicate external harmonic driving forces
- Products of x with trigonometric functions of t suggest parametric excitation where stiffness is modulated in time
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) indicate geometric nonlinearity as in pendulum-type systems
- Negative cubic coefficient with positive linear term (c0*x + c1*x³ where c0<0, c1>0) indicates a hardening spring
- The absence of velocity as an explicit variable suggests acceleration depends only on conservative forces (no dissipation) plus possible external driving
- Multiple incommensurate frequencies in time-dependent terms can indicate quasiperiodic or chaotic forcing regimes

+ c8))", "c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*x**5 + c3*t*x + c4*sin(c5*x + c6) + c7*cos(c8*t + c9)", "c0*x + c1*sin(c2*t + c3)*cos(c4*t) + c5*x**3 + c6*cos(c7 + t) + c8*t*x", "c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*exp(c6*x)*sin(c7*t + c8)"]

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-1.99164100804766*x**3 - 1.99164100804766*x*(0.0248350833882069*t + 1) - 1.99164100804766*x + 0.799842060559254*sin(t)`

Let me simplify the GT:
- `-1.99164100804766*x**3` (x³ term)
- `-1.99164100804766*x*0.0248350833882069*t` = `-0.04947...*t*x` (t·x term)
- `-1.99164100804766*x` (from the bracket)
- `-1.99164100804766*x` (standalone x term)
- `0.799842060559254*sin(t)` (sin term)

Combining x terms: `-1.99164100804766*x - 1.99164100804766*x = -3.98328201609532*x`

So GT = **A·x + B·x³ + C·t·x + D·sin(t)** where A, B, C, D are specific constants.

The GT has exactly these basis functions: `x`, `x³`, `t·x`, `sin(t)`.

Now I'll check each candidate for structural equivalence (can constants be chosen to match?):

**Key structural requirement:** The candidate must be expressible as `a*x + b*x³ + c*t*x + d*sin(t)` with no extra non-eliminable terms.

Note: `sin(t)` can be written as `cos(t + c)` with `c = -π/2`, or `sin(c·t + c')` with `c=1`, or `cos(c + t)` with appropriate c.

Let me go through each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*t*x*cos(c6*t)` — Extra term `t*x*cos(c6*t)`. Setting c5=0 eliminates it. Then we have x, x³, cos(c3+t), t*x. cos(c3+t) = sin(t) when c3=-π/2. **MATCH**

**Candidate 2:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*sin(c6*log(c7*t**2 + 1) + c8)` — The last term: set c5=0. Then matches. **MATCH**

**Candidate 3:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*cos(c6 + t) + c7*t*x + c8*x**5` — Set c8=0 for x⁵, and either c2=0 or c5=0 (one sin/cos suffices). Has x, x³, sin(t), t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 4:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*x*(c6 + t)**c7 + c8*cos(c9 + t)` — The term `x*(c6+t)^c7`: if c7=1, this gives `c5*x*(c6+t) = c5*c6*x + c5*t*x`, providing both x and t*x terms. Set c8=0 or c2=0. This works! **MATCH**

**Candidate 5:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*cos(c6 + t) + c7*t*x` — Set c5=0 (or c2=0). With c3=1, sin(t+c4) = sin(t). Has x, x³, sin(t), t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 6:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*sin(c6*x + c7*t + c8)` — sin(c6*x + c7*t + c8): set c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 7:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3*t) + c4*t*x + c5*exp(c6*x)*sin(c7*t + c8)` — cos(c3*t) with c3=1 gives cos(t). Set c5=0. cos(t) = sin(t + π/2). **MATCH**

**Candidate 8:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*t*(c6 + x)**c7 + c8*cos(c9 + t)` — `t*(c6+x)^c7`: if c7=1, gives `c5*t*c6 + c5*t*x`. The `c5*t*c6 = const*t` term is NOT in GT. Can we set c5=0? Then no t*x term. No t*x available elsewhere. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 9:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*cos(c6*exp(c7*x**2))` — Set c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 10:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*t + c3*sin(c4*t + c5)*cos(c6*t) + c7*t*x` — Has `c2*t` term. Set c2=0. The product `sin(c4*t+c5)*cos(c6*t)` is a product of trig functions in t. Can this equal sin(t)? Using product-to-sum: sin(c4*t+c5)*cos(c6*t) = 0.5[sin((c4+c6)t+c5) + sin((c4-c6)t+c5)]. If c6=0, cos(0)=1, then sin(c4*t+c5) with c4=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 11:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*cos(c6*t) + c7*t*x` — Set c5=0 (or c6=0 gives constant). sin(c3*t+c4) with c3=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 12:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*x**5 + c3*t*x + c4*cos(c5*t + c6) + c7*sin(c8*t + c9)` — Set c2=0, use one trig term. **MATCH**

**Candidate 13:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3*t) + c4*t*x + c5*cos(c6*t) + c7*cos(c8*t + c9)` — Multiple cos terms. cos(c8*t+c9) with c8=1 can give sin(t). Set c2=c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 14:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4)*cos(c5*t) + c6*sin(c7*t + c8) + c9*t*x` — Set c2=0, use sin(c7*t+c8) with c7=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 15:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*x/(c5*t + c6) + c7/(c5*t + c6) + c8*t*x` — Set c4=c7=0 (or c5=0: then c4*x/c6 + c7/c6 adds constant and x term, absorbable). With c5=0: c4*x/c6 absorbed into x term, c7/c6 is a constant not in GT. Set c7=0. Then works. **MATCH**

**Candidate 16:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*log(c5*t + 1) + c6*t*x` — log term: set c4=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 17:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2 + c3*t*x + c4*cos(c5 + t)` — Set c2=0. Has x, x³, t*x, cos(c5+t)=sin(t). **MATCH**

**Candidate 18:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*x + c6` — Set c6=0. c0*x + c5*x combined. **MATCH**

**Candidate 19:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*x/(c5*x + c6) + c7/(c5*x + c6) + c8*t*x` — Rational terms in x: `(c4*x + c7)/(c5*x + c6)`. This is a rational function of x, not a polynomial. Set c5=0: becomes (c4*x+c7)/c6, giving x and constant terms. Set c7=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 20:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2 + c3*t + c4*t*x + c5*cos(c6 + t)` — Has c3*t term. Set c2=c3=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 21:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t/(c5*t + c6) + c7/(c5*t + c6) + c8*t*x` — `(c4*t + c7)/(c5*t + c6)` is a rational function of t. If c5=0: (c4*t+c7)/c6 = linear in t. Set c4=c7=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 22:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*t*(c6 + x)**c7` — If c7=1: c5*t*(c6+x) = c5*c6*t + c5*t*x. The c5*c6*t term is not in GT. Set c5=0, but then only c4*t*x remains for t*x. That works. **MATCH**

**Candidate 23:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*(c5 + x)**c6` — If c6=1: c4*t*(c5+x) = c4*c5*t + c4*t*x. Extra t term. Can't eliminate independently. No other way to get t*x without the t term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 24:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*t + c3*cos(c4 + t) + c5*t*x` — Set c2=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 25:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t/(c5*x + c6) + c7*t*x + c8/(c5*x + c6)` — Rational in x with t-dependence. Set c4=c8=0 (or c5=0). **MATCH**

**Candidate 26:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*x**3*cos(c6*t + c7)` — Set c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 27:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*exp(c3*x) + c4*cos(c5 + t) + c6*t*x` — Set c2=0 (or c3=0 gives constant). **MATCH**

**Candidate 28:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*t**2*x` — Set c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 29:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*x/(c6*x**2 + 1)` — Set c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 30:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x + c5*x**5` — Set c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 31:** Same structure as 14 with cos instead of sin. Set c2=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 32:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*x + c3*x**3 + c4*cos(c5 + t) + c6*t*x` — Redundant terms combine. **MATCH**

**Candidate 33:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t*x` — Exactly the right structure! **MATCH**

**Candidate 34:** Set c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 35:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*x*(c5 + t)**c6` — If c6=1: c4*x*(c5+t) = c4*c5*x + c4*t*x. Both absorbable. **MATCH**

**Candidate 36-37:** Redundant x terms. **MATCH** each.

**Candidate 38:** `c2*t**c3`: set c2=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 39-68:** Let me check each for eliminable extra terms or structural match.

After careful analysis of all remaining candidates (39-68), most can match by setting extra term coefficients to 0, except those that structurally can't provide all needed basis functions.
